{"parentUuid":"cfab3b2d-776a-41f9-a691-76bd8ea608ee","isSidechain":true,"userType":"external","cwd":"/Volumes/ThunderBolt/Development/skippy-agentspace","sessionId":"dadcb58c-add2-43d8-8385-987c1c94baf2","version":"2.1.71","gitBranch":"wip/initial-setup","agentId":"ad01f0808ff72b78e","slug":"linear-juggling-hanrahan","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_vrtx_01M7XLwS3f8BiPEExcztotmy","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Custom Skill System\n     2→\n     3→**The MANDATORY configuration system for ALL skills.**\n     4→\n     5→---\n     6→\n     7→## THIS IS THE AUTHORITATIVE SOURCE\n     8→\n     9→This document defines the **required structure** for every skill in the system.\n    10→\n    11→**ALL skill creation MUST follow this structure** - including skills created by the CreateSkill skill.\n    12→\n    13→**\"Canonicalize a skill\"** = Restructure it to match this exact format, including TitleCase naming.\n    14→\n    15→---\n    16→\n    17→## TitleCase Naming Convention (MANDATORY)\n    18→\n    19→**All naming in the skill system MUST use TitleCase (PascalCase).**\n    20→\n    21→| Component | Wrong | Correct |\n    22→|-----------|-------|---------|\n    23→| Skill directory | `createskill`, `create-skill`, `CREATE_SKILL` | `Createskill` or `CreateSkill` |\n    24→| Workflow files | `create.md`, `update-info.md`, `SYNC_REPO.md` | `Create.md`, `UpdateInfo.md`, `SyncRepo.md` |\n    25→| Reference docs | `prosody-guide.md`, `API_REFERENCE.md` | `ProsodyGuide.md`, `ApiReference.md` |\n    26→| Tool files | `manage-server.ts`, `MANAGE_SERVER.ts` | `ManageServer.ts` |\n    27→| Help files | `manage-server.help.md` | `ManageServer.help.md` |\n    28→| YAML name | `name: create-skill` | `name: CreateSkill` |\n    29→\n    30→**TitleCase Rules:**\n    31→- First letter of each word capitalized\n    32→- No hyphens, underscores, or spaces\n    33→- No ALL_CAPS or all_lowercase\n    34→- Single words: first letter capital (e.g., `Research`, `Art`)\n    35→- Multi-word: each word capitalized, no separator (e.g., `UpdateInfo`, `SyncRepo`)\n    36→\n    37→**Exception:** `SKILL.md` is always uppercase (convention for the main skill file).\n    38→\n    39→---\n    40→\n    41→## The Required Structure\n    42→\n    43→Every SKILL.md has two parts:\n    44→\n    45→### 1. YAML Frontmatter (Single-Line Description)\n    46→\n    47→```yaml\n    48→---\n    49→name: SkillName\n    50→description: [What it does]. USE WHEN [intent triggers using OR]. [Additional capabilities].\n    51→---\n    52→```\n    53→\n    54→**Rules:**\n    55→- `name` uses **TitleCase**\n    56→- `description` is a **single line** (not multi-line with `|`)\n    57→- `USE WHEN` keyword is **MANDATORY** (Claude Code parses this for skill activation)\n    58→- Use intent-based triggers with `OR` for multiple conditions\n    59→- Max 1024 characters (hard limit)\n    60→- **NO separate `triggers:` or `workflows:` arrays in YAML**\n    61→\n    62→### 2. Markdown Body (Workflow Routing + Examples + Documentation)\n    63→\n    64→```markdown\n    65→# SkillName\n    66→\n    67→[Brief description of what the skill does]\n    68→\n    69→## Workflow Routing\n    70→\n    71→| Workflow | Trigger | File |\n    72→|----------|---------|------|\n    73→| **WorkflowOne** | \"trigger phrase\" | `Workflows/WorkflowOne.md` |\n    74→| **WorkflowTwo** | \"another trigger\" | `Workflows/WorkflowTwo.md` |\n    75→\n    76→## Examples\n    77→\n    78→**Example 1: [Common use case]**\n    79→\\`\\`\\`\n    80→User: \"[Typical user request]\"\n    81→→ Invokes WorkflowOne workflow\n    82→→ [What skill does]\n    83→→ [What user gets back]\n    84→\\`\\`\\`\n    85→\n    86→**Example 2: [Another use case]**\n    87→\\`\\`\\`\n    88→User: \"[Another typical request]\"\n    89→→ [Process]\n    90→→ [Output]\n    91→\\`\\`\\`\n    92→\n    93→## [Additional Sections]\n    94→\n    95→[Documentation, quick reference, critical paths, etc.]\n    96→```\n    97→\n    98→**Workflow routing format:** Table with Workflow, Trigger, File columns\n    99→- Workflow names in **TitleCase** matching file names\n   100→- Simple trigger description\n   101→- File path in backticks\n   102→\n   103→---\n   104→\n   105→## Dynamic Loading Pattern (Recommended for Large Skills)\n   106→\n   107→**Purpose:** Reduce context on skill invocation by keeping SKILL.md minimal and loading additional context files only when needed.\n   108→\n   109→### How Loading Works\n   110→\n   111→**Session Startup:**\n   112→- Only frontmatter (YAML) loads from all SKILL.md files for routing\n   113→\n   114→**Skill Invocation:**\n   115→- Full SKILL.md body loads when skill is invoked\n   116→- Additional .md context files load when referenced by workflows or called directly\n   117→\n   118→**Benefit:** Most skill invocations don't need all documentation - load only what workflows actually use.\n   119→\n   120→### The Pattern\n   121→\n   122→**SKILL.md** = Minimal routing + quick reference (30-50 lines)\n   123→**Additional .md files** = Context files - SOPs for specific aspects (loaded on-demand)\n   124→\n   125→### Structure\n   126→\n   127→```\n   128→Skills/SkillName/\n   129→├── SKILL.md                    # Minimal routing - loads on invocation\n   130→├── Aesthetic.md                # Context file - SOP for aesthetic handling\n   131→├── Examples.md                 # Context file - SOP for examples\n   132→├── ApiReference.md             # Context file - SOP for API usage\n   133→├── Tools.md                    # Context file - SOP for tool usage\n   134→├── Workflows/                  # Workflow execution files\n   135→│   ├── Create.md\n   136→│   └── Update.md\n   137→└── Tools/                      # Actual CLI tools\n   138→    └── Generate.ts\n   139→```\n   140→\n   141→### CRITICAL: NO Context/ Subdirectory\n   142→\n   143→**NEVER create a Context/ or Docs/ subdirectory.**\n   144→\n   145→The additional .md files ARE the context files. They live **directly in the skill root directory** alongside SKILL.md.\n   146→\n   147→**WRONG (DO NOT DO THIS):**\n   148→```\n   149→Skills/SkillName/\n   150→├── SKILL.md\n   151→└── Context/              ❌ NEVER CREATE THIS DIRECTORY\n   152→    ├── Aesthetic.md\n   153→    └── Examples.md\n   154→```\n   155→\n   156→**CORRECT:**\n   157→```\n   158→Skills/SkillName/\n   159→├── SKILL.md\n   160→├── Aesthetic.md          ✅ Context file in skill root\n   161→└── Examples.md           ✅ Context file in skill root\n   162→```\n   163→\n   164→**The skill directory itself IS the context.**\n   165→\n   166→### Minimal SKILL.md Example\n   167→\n   168→```markdown\n   169→---\n   170→name: Art\n   171→description: Visual content system. USE WHEN art, header images, visualizations, diagrams.\n   172→---\n   173→\n   174→# Art Skill\n   175→\n   176→Complete visual content system using consistent aesthetic.\n   177→\n   178→## Workflow Routing\n   179→\n   180→| Trigger | Workflow |\n   181→|---------|----------|\n   182→| Blog header/editorial | `Workflows/Essay.md` |\n   183→| Technical diagram | `Workflows/TechnicalDiagrams.md` |\n   184→| Mermaid flowchart | `Workflows/Mermaid.md` |\n   185→\n   186→## Quick Reference\n   187→\n   188→**Aesthetic:** Charcoal architectural sketch\n   189→**Model:** your-preferred-model\n   190→**Output:** Always ~/Downloads/ first\n   191→\n   192→**Full Documentation:**\n   193→- Aesthetic guide: `SkillSearch('art aesthetic')` → loads Aesthetic.md\n   194→- Examples: `SkillSearch('art examples')` → loads Examples.md\n   195→```\n   196→\n   197→### When To Use\n   198→\n   199→Use dynamic loading for skills with:\n   200→- ✅ SKILL.md > 100 lines\n   201→- ✅ Multiple documentation sections\n   202→- ✅ Extensive API reference\n   203→- ✅ Detailed examples\n   204→- ✅ Tool documentation\n   205→\n   206→Don't bother for:\n   207→- ❌ Simple skills (< 50 lines total)\n   208→- ❌ Pure utility wrappers\n   209→\n   210→---\n   211→\n   212→## Directory Structure\n   213→\n   214→Every skill follows this structure:\n   215→\n   216→```\n   217→SkillName/                    # TitleCase directory name\n   218→├── SKILL.md                  # Main skill file (always uppercase)\n   219→├── QuickStartGuide.md        # Context/reference files in root (TitleCase)\n   220→├── Examples.md               # Context/reference files in root (TitleCase)\n   221→├── Tools/                    # CLI tools (ALWAYS present, even if empty)\n   222→│   ├── ToolName.ts           # TypeScript CLI tool (TitleCase)\n   223→│   └── ToolName.help.md      # Tool documentation (TitleCase)\n   224→└── Workflows/                # Work execution workflows (TitleCase)\n   225→    ├── Create.md             # Workflow file\n   226→    ├── UpdateInfo.md         # Workflow file\n   227→    └── SyncRepo.md           # Workflow file\n   228→```\n   229→\n   230→---\n   231→\n   232→## Flat Folder Structure (MANDATORY)\n   233→\n   234→**CRITICAL: Keep folder structure FLAT - maximum 2 levels deep.**\n   235→\n   236→### The Rule\n   237→\n   238→Skills use a **flat hierarchy** - no deep nesting of subdirectories.\n   239→\n   240→**Maximum depth:** `Skills/SkillName/Category/`\n   241→\n   242→### ALLOWED (2 levels max)\n   243→\n   244→```\n   245→Skills/Research/SKILL.md                        # Skill root\n   246→Skills/Research/Workflows/DeepDive.md           # Workflow - one level deep\n   247→Skills/Research/Tools/Analyze.ts                # Tool - one level deep\n   248→Skills/Research/Examples.md                     # Context file - in root\n   249→```\n   250→\n   251→### FORBIDDEN (Too deep OR wrong location)\n   252→\n   253→```\n   254→Skills/Research/Resources/Examples.md           # Context files go in root, NOT Resources/\n   255→Skills/Research/Workflows/Category/Deep.md      # THREE levels - NO\n   256→Skills/Research/Tools/Utils/Helper.ts           # THREE levels - NO\n   257→```\n   258→\n   259→### Why Flat Structure\n   260→\n   261→1. **Discoverability** - Easy to find files with simple `ls` or `grep`\n   262→2. **Simplicity** - Less cognitive overhead navigating directories\n   263→3. **Speed** - Faster file operations without deep traversal\n   264→4. **Maintainability** - Harder to create organizational complexity\n   265→5. **Consistency** - Every skill follows same simple pattern\n   266→\n   267→---\n   268→\n   269→## Examples Section (REQUIRED)\n   270→\n   271→**Every skill MUST have an `## Examples` section** showing 2-3 concrete usage patterns.\n   272→\n   273→**Why Examples Matter:**\n   274→- Examples improve tool selection accuracy from 72% to 90%\n   275→- Descriptions tell the AI WHEN to activate; examples show HOW the skill works\n   276→- The AI learns the full input→behavior→output pattern, not just trigger keywords\n   277→\n   278→**Example Format:**\n   279→```markdown\n   280→## Examples\n   281→\n   282→**Example 1: [Use case name]**\n   283→\\`\\`\\`\n   284→User: \"[Actual user request]\"\n   285→→ Invokes WorkflowName workflow\n   286→→ [What the skill does - action 1]\n   287→→ [What user receives back]\n   288→\\`\\`\\`\n   289→\n   290→**Example 2: [Another use case]**\n   291→\\`\\`\\`\n   292→User: \"[Different request pattern]\"\n   293→→ [Process steps]\n   294→→ [Output/result]\n   295→\\`\\`\\`\n   296→```\n   297→\n   298→**Guidelines:**\n   299→- Use 2-3 examples per skill (not more)\n   300→- Show realistic user requests\n   301→- Include the workflow or action taken (TitleCase)\n   302→- Show what output/result the user gets\n   303→- Cover the most common use cases\n   304→\n   305→---\n   306→\n   307→## Intent Matching, Not String Matching\n   308→\n   309→We use **intent matching**, not exact phrase matching.\n   310→\n   311→**Example description:**\n   312→```yaml\n   313→description: Complete research workflow. USE WHEN user mentions research, investigation, deep dive, analyze topic, or gather information on something.\n   314→```\n   315→\n   316→**Key Principles:**\n   317→- Use intent language: \"user mentions\", \"user wants to\", \"including things like\"\n   318→- Don't list exact phrases in quotes\n   319→- Cover the domain conceptually\n   320→- Use `OR` to combine multiple trigger conditions\n   321→\n   322→---\n   323→\n   324→## Workflow-to-Tool Integration\n   325→\n   326→**Workflows should map user intent to tool flags, not hardcode single invocation patterns.**\n   327→\n   328→When a workflow calls a CLI tool, it should:\n   329→1. **Interpret user intent** from the request\n   330→2. **Consult flag mapping tables** to determine appropriate flags\n   331→3. **Construct the CLI command** with selected flags\n   332→4. **Execute and handle results**\n   333→\n   334→### Intent-to-Flag Mapping Tables\n   335→\n   336→Workflows should include tables that map natural language intent to CLI flags:\n   337→\n   338→```markdown\n   339→## Model Selection\n   340→\n   341→| User Says | Flag | Use Case |\n   342→|-----------|------|----------|\n   343→| \"fast\", \"quick\" | `--model haiku` | Speed priority |\n   344→| \"best\", \"highest quality\" | `--model opus` | Quality priority |\n   345→| (default) | `--model sonnet` | Balanced default |\n   346→\n   347→## Output Options\n   348→\n   349→| User Says | Flag | Effect |\n   350→|-----------|------|--------|\n   351→| \"JSON output\" | `--format json` | Machine-readable |\n   352→| \"detailed\" | `--verbose` | Extra information |\n   353→| \"just the result\" | `--quiet` | Minimal output |\n   354→```\n   355→\n   356→---\n   357→\n   358→## CLI Tools (tools/ directory)\n   359→\n   360→**Every skill MUST have a `Tools/` directory**, even if empty. CLI tools automate repetitive tasks.\n   361→\n   362→### When to Create a CLI Tool\n   363→\n   364→Create CLI tools for:\n   365→- **Server management** - start, stop, restart, status\n   366→- **State queries** - check if running, get configuration\n   367→- **Repeated operations** - tasks executed frequently by workflows\n   368→- **Complex automation** - multi-step processes that benefit from encapsulation\n   369→\n   370→### Tool Requirements\n   371→\n   372→Every CLI tool must:\n   373→1. **Be TypeScript** - Use `#!/usr/bin/env bun` shebang\n   374→2. **Use TitleCase naming** - `ToolName.ts`, not `tool-name.ts`\n   375→3. **Have a help file** - `ToolName.help.md` with full documentation\n   376→4. **Support `--help`** - Display usage information\n   377→5. **Use colored output** - ANSI colors for terminal feedback\n   378→6. **Handle errors gracefully** - Clear error messages, appropriate exit codes\n   379→\n   380→---\n   381→\n   382→## Complete Checklist\n   383→\n   384→Before a skill is complete:\n   385→\n   386→### Naming (TitleCase)\n   387→- [ ] Skill directory uses TitleCase (e.g., `Research`, `Art`)\n   388→- [ ] YAML `name:` uses TitleCase\n   389→- [ ] All workflow files use TitleCase (e.g., `Create.md`, `UpdateInfo.md`)\n   390→- [ ] All reference docs use TitleCase (e.g., `ApiReference.md`)\n   391→- [ ] All tool files use TitleCase (e.g., `Analyze.ts`)\n   392→- [ ] Routing table workflow names match file names exactly\n   393→\n   394→### YAML Frontmatter\n   395→- [ ] Single-line `description` with embedded `USE WHEN` clause\n   396→- [ ] No separate `triggers:` or `workflows:` arrays\n   397→- [ ] Description uses intent-based language\n   398→- [ ] Description under 1024 characters\n   399→\n   400→### Markdown Body\n   401→- [ ] `## Workflow Routing` section with table format\n   402→- [ ] All workflow files have routing entries\n   403→- [ ] **`## Examples` section with 2-3 concrete usage patterns** (REQUIRED)\n   404→\n   405→### Structure\n   406→- [ ] `Tools/` directory exists (even if empty)\n   407→- [ ] No `backups/` directory inside skill\n   408→- [ ] Workflows contain ONLY work execution procedures\n   409→- [ ] Reference docs live at skill root (not in Workflows/)\n   410→\n   411→---\n   412→\n   413→## Skill Discovery: SkillsMP\n   414→\n   415→**SkillsMP.com** - Centralized directory of 87,427+ Claude Code skills\n   416→\n   417→### Overview\n   418→\n   419→- **What it is:** Aggregated skill repository from GitHub\n   420→- **Categories:** Tools, Development, Data & AI, Business, DevOps, Testing & Security, Content & Media, Documentation, Research, Databases, Lifestyle, Blockchain\n   421→- **Search:** AI semantic search powered by Cloudflare\n   422→- **Preview:** SKILL.md preview before installation\n   423→- **Cross-platform:** Works with Claude Code, Codex CLI, ChatGPT\n   424→\n   425→### Installation Methods\n   426→\n   427→**Global install:**\n   428→```bash\n   429→npx skills add vercel/next.js\n   430→```\n   431→\n   432→**Local download:**\n   433→Download ZIP, extract to `~/.claude/skills/`\n   434→\n   435→**CLI (with marketplace.json):**\n   436→Direct installation through Claude Code plugin system\n   437→\n   438→### Quality Validation (IMPORTANT)\n   439→\n   440→⚠️ **No quality validation** - Skills are scraped from GitHub without testing\n   441→\n   442→**Before installing:**\n   443→1. Read SKILL.md preview carefully\n   444→2. Check for clear documentation\n   445→3. Verify it matches your needs\n   446→4. Test in isolated environment first\n   447→5. Review code for security concerns\n   448→\n   449→**Rating system:** Planned but not yet implemented\n   450→\n   451→### When to Use SkillsMP\n   452→\n   453→**Good for:**\n   454→- ✅ Discovering existing solutions\n   455→- ✅ Finding inspiration for new skills\n   456→- ✅ Exploring common patterns\n   457→- ✅ Quick prototyping\n   458→\n   459→**Not recommended for:**\n   460→- ❌ Production use without validation\n   461→- ❌ Trusting without code review\n   462→- ❌ Assuming quality/security\n   463→\n   464→### Best Practices\n   465→\n   466→1. **Evaluate first** - Read SKILL.md thoroughly\n   467→2. **Test isolated** - Try in non-production environment\n   468→3. **Adapt** - Use as starting point, customize to needs\n   469→4. **Contribute back** - Share improvements with community\n   470→5. **Follow PAI standards** - Canonicalize to TitleCase structure\n   471→\n   472→---\n   473→\n   474→**Repository:** SkillsMP.com\n   475→**Count:** 87,427+ skills (as of Jan 2026)\n   476→**Growth:** ~800 skills per period average\n   477→**Peak:** 20,218 skills added on Jan 22, 2026\n   478→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Identify the current project's `.planning/` directory\n    36→2. Find the most recently completed phase (check STATE.md or scan `phases/` dirs)\n    37→3. Read the phase's `PLAN.md` for planned tasks and acceptance criteria\n    38→4. Read the phase's `SUMMARY.md` (or execution output) for actual results\n    39→5. Compare:\n    40→   - Which tasks completed vs skipped vs added mid-flight?\n    41→   - Which acceptance criteria passed vs failed vs untested?\n    42→   - Any files changed that weren't in the plan?\n    43→6. Output a reconciliation report (see `references/reconciliation.md` for template)\n    44→7. If STATE.md or PROJECT.md have drifted, flag the misalignment\n    45→\n    46→**Output:** Reconciliation report printed to terminal. Run `~/.config/pai/Skills/skippy-dev/bin/skippy-update.sh`\n    55→2. Review the diff report\n    56→3. Human decides what to absorb -- no auto-merge\n    57→\n    58→### `/skippy:cleanup`\n    59→\n    60→Manage ephemeral files (debug logs, telemetry, session history).\n    61→\n    62→**Workflow:**\n    63→\n    64→1. Reports space freed\n    67→\n    68→## For Agents\n    69→\n    70→When spawning GSD agents (planner, executor, verifier), you can enhance their prompts:\n    71→\n    72→```\n    73→Read ~/.config/pai/Skills/skippy-dev/references/task-anatomy.md\n    74→# Include when the agent is creating plans\n    75→\n    76→Read ~/.config/pai/Skills/skippy-dev/references/plan-boundaries.md\n    77→# Include when the plan needs scope protection\n    78→\n    79→Read ~/.config/pai/Skills/skippy-dev/references/state-consistency.md\n    80→# Include when the agent touches state files\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
